  32. I owned one of these for a while until it broke, then I got the same one again. I like the versatility and that it is so easy to clean and rinse under water. The only caveat is that the hair can clog the trimmer, and to clean it the adjustable guard needs to be removed. When you put the guard back on to continue, it is easy to dial in a wrong (too short) setting by accident. But eventually I learned to look out for that.<br /><br />Now here is the reason why I am writing this review: The rechargeable battery on my trimmer was getting progressively worse, so I decided to try and replace it. It is possible to carefully open the trimmer with the right screwdrivers. Inside, you will discover a single NiCd AA cell. I tested it with my trusty LaCrosse charger, and was told it had around 580mAh capacity left, which was barely enough to last through a single use of the trimmer. Also, the battery would usually self-discharge in a day or two, and combined with the very slow charger, it meant that I needed to charge the trimmer a day or so in advance to actually use it.<br /><br />I removed the NiCd AA cell and soldered a single NiMH AA Eneloop in its place instead. This new cell has around 1850mAh and virtually no self-discharge. This means the shaver will now run 3x as long as before, and when I leave it in the drawer for a week or a month, it will not have lost its charge. The motor turns faster too. I took some care to make sure that the case was properly water-proofed again during assembly, and all is well now.<br /><br />Why can't Panasonic put a good battery into their trimmers to begin with?

  84. I bought this shaver Nov. 2011 and have NOT broken the comb attachment. Allow me to explain how I do it.<br />To remove the comb attachment:<br />1. Turn the dial to 20. See? It's practically off already.<br />2. Hold shaver in your right hand hand with right thumb at the bottom right of the comb attachment. Push up with your thumb while gently holding the comb attachment with your left hand and pulling up and guiding with left hand.<br />3. Easy peasy.<br /><br />To replace the comb attachment:<br />1. Turn the dial to 1.<br />2. Slide the comb attachment on. It's almost on already at this point. Only about 1/8-inch to go.<br />3. Gently press down until it snaps into place.<br /><br />I'm buying another trimmer because the battery isn't holding a charge for very long anymore and it'll just be a matter of time until it dies. The old comb attachment appears to be interchangeable with the new one so I've got a spare now.<br /><br />If my instructions aren't clear enough, let me know and I'll try to improve them.

  148. Having used a Norelco model for years, but frustrated with how quickly the non-replaceable batteries wear out, I decided to give this Panasonic a try. For one thing, the comb attachment seems very flimsy, and requires a good yank to remove it. It slides into a little notch on the trimmer, and I have some serious doubts that it's going to last very long before breaking. Another inconvenience is that you have to turn the trimmer off in order to adjust the comb height. Plus, unlike the Norelco which has a built in charge meter, so that you know when the charge is complete, or when you're about the run out of juice, the Panasonic just has a simple charge light that provides no info at all. Finally, the Norelco's comb attachment flexed to fit the contours of your face or head, while the Panasonic's comb attachment is fixed. In my opinion, the flexible attachment on the Norelco was able to provide a closer and more even cut. All in all, maybe for a Panasonic model, this is a good trimmer; I really can't say because I haven't owned a Panasonic before. But compared to the Norelco, well, there really isn't any comparison. Like I said, it is half the price of the Norelco, but I guess you get what you pay for.

Making it nearly impossible for the hair to get to the clippers. Next, the clipper blade is not parallel to the guard! I have no idea who designed that, but the blade should be parallel to the surface of the skin. And therefore the guard should be parallel to both. The guard also has teeth that cover both sides. Forming a cage that traps the hair. The guard must be removed ever few seconds. Which makes it feel like it is going to break. And it resets it's number setting. Which is another thing. For cleaning the components of hair, skin, and oil debris, as well as for sharpening.<br /><br />I cut my hair twice a month or so.   212. VERDICT: Good trimmer that is worthly of the Panasonic name, but keep the receipt just in case you don't like the design. PROS: - Quiet - Sharp blades - Light weight - Versatile Wet/Dry design - Excellent battery life (holds a charge for weeks at a time) - Compact design - Single height adjustment (no need for multiple attachments) - Reasonable price CONS: - Mini trimmer involves removing plastic beard height attachment - Beard height attachment removal procedure must be performed a specific way to prevent damage - Does not groom all hair at consistent height on shortest setting on my face SUMMARY: I've purchased two of these trimmers over the past few years. One stays home and the other is for travel. I can recommend this trimmer, but it does take some time to get familiar with how to manipulate it for a consistent trim. I've only used it on my anchor beard and some body hair. It works fine for both. Use a light touch with this trimmer. If the height adjustment piece is removed, be warned that you will eventually get cut if trimming a very contoured part of your face or body. The mini trimmer behind the main trimmer is nice for ear and nose hair, but don't press too hard or it will cut into your skin. It's nice to know that it is a Wet/Dry design (no need to worry about shocks or rust,) but I prefer Dry and can't comment on Wet performance. Keeping the blades lubricated once a month to maintain sharpness will easily double the life of the blades and improve overall performance. ATTACHMENT REMOVAL PROCEDURE: Extend the attachment by turning the adjustment wheel to the highest numerical setting. Grab the corner of the attachment that is directly above the plastic adjustment slider that moves horizontally when the dial is turned. In the same motion, pull up on the corner while pulling the attachment away from the trimmer. ATTACHMENT REINSTALLATION PROCEDURE: Turn the adjustment wheel to the lowest numerical setting. Replacethe attachment by aligning it with the trimmer and slide back until you reach the horizontal adjustment slider. With a quick motion, push the attachment into the horizontal slider. It will click into place without harm to the trimmer.

  316. Several years ago I purchased a Panasonic C282 trimmer which, at the time, was the only cordless hair trimmer I could find. I had to get it from Canada as it wasn't marketed in the US. I wanted a cordless because I found it cumbersome using a corded trimmer to do my own hair. I just bought the ER224S as my C282 recently broke after I carelessly dropped it. I just used the new trimmer and have to say, I feel pretty good about it... Since my old trimmer had broken, my hair was much longer than usual and the new trimmer had no problem going through it, as some other reviews suggested. I did have to stop a couple of times and remove the comb to clear out the built up hair, but that won't be a problem if you keep your hair short. The old trimmer had a smaller comb and it was easier to flick the cut hair out of it without having to remove it but this seems minor unless you are often cutting long hair, which I do not. That is the only slight knock I can give the new trimmer compared to the old one. Otherwise the motor seems stronger and quieter on the newer one. The larger comb and cutting head is easier to hold and I like the adjustment knob better than the slider on the old trimmer. Despite some reviews it does not seem easy to accidentally change settings in use as it seems to lock down the setting once the power is on. The old trimmer could occasionally slip settings during use, though it wasn't too bad - the new trimmer seems to improve on that as well. The setting numbering seems odd as they have 1, 2, 5, 8, 11, 14, 17 and 20, with half step settings between each position. The 2 setting is roughly equivalent to the 2 setting on my old trimmer and the 5 seems to be about what the old trimmer's 3 was so I don't understand why they didn't just number them sequentially. I personally do not like traditional corded trimmers with separate attachments for each length. I had a Conair trimmer for a while and just didn't like it. It is much more convenient todial in my desired cutting length instead of having to switch out different combs for each length step. Cutting without the cord is much easier as well, obviously. So I am very happy with this trimmer so far and would recommend it.<br /><br />**** Update about 10 years later!!<br /><br />So I have been using this trimmer since 2007! It is a great trimmer and I just purchased it again because the original one finally died outright. Not bad I say for 10 years. So my experience with this trimmer has revealed two things to look out for.<br /><br />Firstly, as some reviews have mentioned, the plastic comb can break. If you drop the trimmer, the comb will probably break depending on how it lands. I have only dropped my trimmer once in 10 years so unless you are a klutz, I don't think that's a big issue. However, if you take the comb off incorrectly it can also break. The comb clips in on one side but the other side kind of free floats a bit. If you pull from the free floating side and are not careful, you can can cause it to crack. I have found if I only pull on the connected side and do so with firm but careful pressure, it comes off easily without breaking so this isn't really an issue either. Also replacement combs are relatively cheap I keep an extra one or two just in case but haven't had to replace them very often at all.<br /><br />The other issue, also mentioned in a bunch of reviews, is that the battery in the trimmer does not last forever. Shouldn't be a surprise, rechargeable batteries only have about a 2-3 year expected life in general. Should Panasonic have made it easier to replace the battery? Sure, but I don't put too much of a knock on this trimmer because of it. If you want, you can get a replacement battery if you search. And while not very easy, it is possible to replace the battery. My experience was that the battery lasted a decently long 5-7 years. I don't remember exactly when it stopped taking a full charge but I did use it forthe last 3-4 years as mostly a corded trimmer and it was still a good experience. However, just this past week it stopped turning on at all. It appeared to be fully charged, but wouldn't turn on even while corded.<br /><br />So I looked at a bunch of different trimmers but realized for the price, under $30 now, it is such a great trimmer that I decided to just go ahead and order it again. The one thing I don't like about this model now is that it came with only the stand charger and not the cord. So when the battery does go you can't use it as a corded trimmer. For me that's not an issue because I saved my cord from the first one and it still fits the new one. Anyway, a great trimmer. Highly recommended!!

Some of the user comments on Amazon did not affect me and I felt compelled to tell about it: <br /> <br />1. Binding. Just keep your hair short and trim often and it won't bind. What else can you expect from a cordless trimmer. They do not put out power compared to a corded electric one. Even with the trimmer plugged in, it still will bind. I found this out the very first time I used it. My hair was about 1 1/2 inches long. Yes, it did bind (the first time). After keeping my hair at setting 8 (roughly 1/4 inch), it does not bind anymore. <br /> <br />2. Setting dial gets accidently turned. I never had a problem. Besides, the way I hold the shaver my thumb is permanently planted on the dial anyway so it will prevent it from turning. The other reviewers who had this problem may have been holding it the wrong way. It does require a little finesse, but you'll get the hang of it by the second or third time. <br /> <br />3. Ease of cleaning. The description does not lie when it says submersible. Easy to clean removable blades. Water does not affect this trimmer at all. Very good water-proof design by Panasonic. <br /> <br />4. Comes with a little oil bottle and small brush. I clean the thing every single time I use it so it's ready to go the next time. Just oil the blades after every use (Panasonic recommended oiling before and after). I found too much oil will make it harder to clean because the hair sticks more and water can't simply wash it out. <br /> <br />3. Overall this trimmer is good to go. Will save me a lot of $ during my 1 year deployment. Plus the good thing is I don't have to wait in line anymore to get a 5 minute haircut!!! <br /> <br />Hope this helps.

  387. This trimmer works great, cuts better than expected, and operates with a minimum of noise. I've trimmed my beard and cut my scalp hair several times. And, the cutting action is very effective with no snagging or pulling of hair - utterly ouchless. Combine this with the quiet operation and I will have to agree with another review that this is ideal for cutting children's hair, leaving them nothing to be afraid of.<br /><br />The only major problem I have with this trimmer is that it has no path for hair clippings. They quickly collect inside the guard and hinder cutting performance unless continuously emptied every 10 to 30 seconds. On a light beard, this might equate to only 1 or 2 interruptions per trim. But, when clipping scalp hair, it makes for a very busy session.<br /><br />I will reiterate another review by saying that removing the guard is less than intuitive or easy. But, success using a suggested technique makes in manageable. The technique involves leaving the trimmer on while removing the guard. Leaving it on effectively locks the guard pin from moving with the guard while removing and reattaching it.<br /><br />Technique for Easier Guard Removal<br /><br />While the trimmer is on, clasp the trimmer upright in both palms with the dial facing you. Place your thumbs on both corners of the guard closest to the dial and push the guard outward (away from you) using your thumbs. You should hear the guard pin click once released. Then you can easily pull the guard off. One quick shake of both the guard and trimmer should release any clumps of hair clippings. Reattaching the guard should be easy enough. Just listen for the guard pin to click back into a secured position.<br /><br />Note: If you use the trimmer on the shortest setting, you may find it difficult to get your thumbs behind the corners of the guard for a push. So, I recommend a minimum setting of 5 while removing the guard.
